width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT FOUR: COMMUNICABLE DISEASES</p>
<p>In this unit, you will explore the common communicable diseases found in this country. The unit is divided into eight sections. In section one and two you will cover patterns and principles of communicable diseases, respectively. In sections three to eight, you will examine specific communicable diseases classified according to their modes of transmission.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="this-eight-units-are-as-follows">This eight units are as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#this-eight-units-are-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Section One: Patterns of Communicable Diseases</p>
<p>Section Two: Principles of Communicable Disease Control</p>
<p>Section Three: Contact Diseases</p>
<p>Section Four: Vector-borne Diseases</p>
<p>Section Five: Diseases Caused by Faecal-oral Contamination</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-patterns-of-communicable-diseases">SECTION 1: PATTERNS OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-patterns-of-communicable-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In unit three, you covered environmental health and learnt that although the environment can be a source of ill health, you can prevent many diseases and health problems through simple measures such as good personal hygiene and proper waste disposal. However, despite your best efforts, you can still contract diseases from different sources. The common cold is a good example. It takes just one person infected with the flu virus to spread it round to the others in the office or at home. A disease that is passed from one person to another person is called a communicable or transmissible disease. Transmissible diseases include: measles, HIV infection, tuberculosis, chickenpox, gonorrhoea, scabies, malaria, cholera, and roundworms among others.</p>
<p>Communicable diseases are among the most important diseases in this country. They are important because:</p>
<ul>
<li>Many of them are common</li>
<li>Some of them are very serious and cause death and disability</li>
<li>Some of them cause widespread outbreaks of disease – epidemics</li>
<li>Most of them can be prevented by fairly simple means</li>
</ul>
<p>In this section you will cover disease patterns in the community, the meaning of host and infection, as well as the transmission cycle of communicable diseases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the patterns of diseases in the community</li>
<li>Describe the interaction between the host and the infecting agent</li>
<li>Describe a typical transmission cycle</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patterns-of-communicable-diseases-in-the-community">Patterns of Communicable Diseases in the Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patterns-of-communicable-diseases-in-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Different diseases are common in different places and at different times. To understand why this happens, you need to consider the disease causative organisms (the agents);</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>the people they infect (the hosts); and the surroundings in which they live (the environment).</p>
<p>A delicate balance exists between the agent, the host and the environment and it can change in different ways. For instance, the agent needs a suitable environment in which to grow and multiply and thus be able to spread and infect other hosts. If the environment does not support the agent it dies or transforms to a dormant state. The host (person) is also affected by the environment. For example, a person may live in a hot, wet climate where there are many mosquitoes. However they can change this environment by draining swamps, clearing the vegetation and adding competing hosts such as animals. If the balance is shifted against the agent, the disease will be controlled and the number of cases will go down.</p>
<p>When the balance between the agent, the host and the environment is fairly constant, you tend to see approximately the same number of cases of the disease every month. When this happens the disease is said to be endemic. When the balance is shifted in favour of the agent (organism), for example, when many nonimmune children have been born in an area since the last measles epidemic, a large number of cases of measles may occur in a short time. This is called an epidemic. Epidemic diseases occur during certain periods or seasons and cause sudden deaths and much suffering in the community.</p>
<p>An endemic disease can be termed as that which occurs in a given population at a constant rate over a period of several years. An epidemic disease is that which occurs in a population at a higher rate than is usually the normal for that population over a given time interval.</p>
<p>Diagrammatically the endemic and epidemic disease patterns can be illustrated as shown on the right.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-feeb0d51.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-down-three-epidemic-diseases-in-kenya-some-common-epidemic-diseases-in-kenya">List down three epidemic diseases in Kenya. Some Common Epidemic Diseases in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-down-three-epidemic-diseases-in-kenya-some-common-epidemic-diseases-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Typhoid fever</li>
<li>Highland malaria</li>
<li>Acute bacterial meningitis</li>
</ul>
<p>In Kenya, malaria is endemic in the lowlands, such as the Tana River basin, the coastal strip, and the Lake Victoria region. Schistosomiasis which is related to water use is endemic around the Lake Victoria region and the Mwea irrigation scheme. Leishmaniasis is endemic in Baringo, along Tana River, and along the River Athi in Machakos.</p>
<p>In some parts of the country, some disease outbreaks occur only occasionally without a regular pattern. Such diseases are said to be sporadic in their occurrence.</p>
<p>Opposite is a map of Kenya illustrating the malaria patterns.</p>
<p>Now, look at what happens once an infecting organism enters a person's body and causes disease.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-dd494ed0.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-host-and-infection">The Host and Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-host-and-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A person who is invaded by a disease-causing micro-organism is called a host. An infection occurs when this micro-organism begins to reproduce (multiply) and grow. When an organism infects a person, there are three possible stages to consider.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incubation-period">Incubation Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incubation-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incubation period is the time between infection and the appearance of symptoms and signs of an illness. During the incubation period the host does not realise that they have an infection until several days later when detectable symptoms and signs of the illness occur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sub-clinical-infection">Sub-clinical Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sub-clinical-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At this stage, infection does not produce clear signs and symptoms. The host's immune system is trying to fight off the agent.</p>
<p>In some cases, the organism is overcome by the host immune cells hence no signs and symptoms are felt and the infection process is terminated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-infection">Clinical Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the period when the host develops detectable symptoms and signs of an illness. At this time the agent has multiplied within the host overcoming the host's immune system and has started causing abnormal functioning of some body cells and tissues. This produces overt signs and symptoms of the disease.</p>
<p>It is important for you to understand these stages because people with symptoms are easier to identify as they come to your health facilities for treatment. People with sub-clinical infections do not always know they are infected and hence are a danger to other people. They are also difficult to detect in the general population without special tests. An individual who is suffering from a sub-clinical infection is also likely to infect others, as in the case of HIV infection which leads to AIDS after a long period. They are therefore known as carriers. An individual who develops a clinical or sub-clinical infection is said to be susceptible to the disease. A susceptible individual is one whose body lacks resistance to the disease. Resistance of the body to a disease occurs due to various immunity mechanisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="write-down-the-two-types-of-immunity-found-in-our-body">Write down the two types of immunity found in our body.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#write-down-the-two-types-of-immunity-found-in-our-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your answer should have included the following two types of immunity:</p>
<ul>
<li>Natural acquired immunity (passive and active)</li>
<li>Artificially acquired immunity (passive and active)</li>
</ul>
<p>For more information on immunity, read module one, unit three part one, section one, on the organisation of the human body, dysfunctions and management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-disease-transmission-cycle">The Disease Transmission Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-disease-transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A disease transmission cycle is a series of steps that a disease-causing organism undergoes in its disease-causing process.</p>
<p>Disease-causing organisms are living things that need somewhere to live and reproduce. This may be within inanimate or animate environment (example in rodents, insect, or the human body), which is known as the reservoir of infection. The human being is the main reservoir of most of the communicable diseases that affect humanity.</p>
<p>When an infection spreads to a new host, the place, animal or human from which the organism came from is called the source of the infection. The way in which an organism leaves the source (the infected host) and passes to a new susceptible host is called the route of transmission. Each disease-causing organism has particular routes which play a large part in how these organisms spread in the community.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 97 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>For example, some organisms are spread through water and food, while others are spread by vectors like mosquitoes and snails.</p>
<p>The diagram above illustrates the differences between the disease transmission cycle in measles, and in malaria where the causative organism passes from human being to mosquito and back to the human being.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-bbaf66dd.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Every transmission cycle is made up of three parts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-source">The Source<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is where the disease-causing organisms spreads from. It could be an infected person, animal, place, or object. The reservoir is the source of infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="transmission-route">Transmission Route<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-route" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main routes of transmission are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Direct contact, for example sexual contact, contact with skin or mucous membranes</li>
<li>Vectors</li>
<li>Faecal-oral (ingesting contaminated food and water)</li>
<li>Airborne</li>
<li>Transplacental (mother to foetus)</li>
<li>Blood contact (transfusion, surgery, injection)</li>
<li>Contact with animals or their products</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="susceptible-host">Susceptible Host<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#susceptible-host" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An individual who has low resistance to a particular disease is said to be a susceptible host for that disease. There are a number of factors which lower the body's resistance to a disease:</p>
<ul>
<li>Not having come in contact with the disease-causing organisms before and therefore not having any immunity to it. For example, passive immunity against measles is lost at the age of 6 - 12 months. Therefore if a child comes into contact with the measles virus after this age, they may develop the disease.</li>
<li>Having a serious illness like AIDS which suppresses a person's immunity. People with AIDS have a high risk of developing tuberculosis.</li>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
<li>Certain drugs such as those used to treat cancer can lower a person's resistance to disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-principles-of-communicable-disease-control">SECTION 2: PRINCIPLES OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASE CONTROL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-principles-of-communicable-disease-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Welcome to section two. In this section you will look at the main methods (also known as principles) that are used to control the occurrence and spread of communicable diseases. It is a short but intense section which will give you the foundation you need to prevent and control the diseases you shall cover in subsequent sections</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the principles of communicable disease control</li>
<li>Describe the methods used to prevent communicable diseases</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the role of the community members in prevention of communicable diseases</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-communicable-disease-control">Methods of Communicable Disease Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-communicable-disease-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Communicable disease can be controlled and eradicated from the community. When thinking about the control of diseases it is always good to think of all the possible methods. In most cases one or two specific methods will have the greatest effect and should be the focus of your activity, in other cases some methods will be useless against the disease. The aim of control is to tip the balance against the agent.</p>
<p>The control and eradication of communicable diseases can be done by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Attacking the source of the disease-causing organism</li>
<li>Interrupting the transmission route</li>
<li>Protecting the susceptible host</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each method in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="attacking-the-source">Attacking the Source<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attacking-the-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are various specific measures which can be used to control the spread of an infectious disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="they-include">They include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#they-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Treating the infected person or animal with the appropriate antibiotics that destroy the disease causing-organism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treating the carriers and sub-clinical cases after carrying out screening tests among suspected individuals or groups.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treating specific groups of persons who are at high risk of being infected (mass treatment). This is called chemoprophylaxis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Isolating those persons who are infected with highly infectious diseases such as ebola, marburg fever, lassa fever; so as to prevent the spread of the organism to other healthy people.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treating sick animals such as cattle suffering from brucellosis, immunising animals such as cows from anthrax, and dogs from rabies; killing sick animals such as rats to control plague and dogs to prevent rabies; separating humans from animals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Notifying the local health authorities immediately you suspect a patient is suffering from an infectious disease. Though this does not directly affect the source, it is an essential way of keeping watch on the number of new cases and thereby monitoring the effectiveness of the control programme.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>All of the methods mentioned on the previous page are methods of controlling the reservoir - where an animal is the reservoir.</p>
<p>In summary you can state that the measures for attacking the source are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Treating the infected person/s</li>
<li>Treating the carrier</li>
<li>Mass treatment of persons at risk</li>
<li>Isolating the infected person/s</li>
<li>Treating the sick animal such as cows</li>
<li>Immunising animals such as dogs and cattle</li>
<li>Killing the animal reservoir such as rats</li>
<li>Separating humans and animals</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interrupting-the-transmission-cycle">Interrupting the Transmission Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interrupting-the-transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A number of methods are used to interrupt the transmission cycle. Some of the measures were covered in detail in unit three of this module. They include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
<li>Environmental health</li>
<li>Water and sanitation</li>
<li>Vector control</li>
<li>Good and adequate housing</li>
<li>Effective food handling and adequate nutrition</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong> A clean environment and good personal hygiene are the most important measures in the primary prevention of diseases.</p>
<p>Please review each one of these measures in unit three of this module so as to complete this section successfully. In addition to the measures covered in unit three, add sterilisation of medical equipment and the use of sterile surgical equipment. These methods are useful for interrupting the transmission of diseases such as, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) infection and hepatitis-B infection.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 99 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 100 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protecting-the-host">Protecting the Host<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protecting-the-host" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the third principle of controlling the spread of communicable disease in the community. Any person who is not yet infected by a specific disease-causing organism is known as a susceptible host. This is because they are at risk of contracting the infection. All susceptible hosts must be protected from contracting the infection.</p>
<p>Remember: The most effective way of controlling communicable diseases is to use a combination of methods: attacking the source of the infecting organism, interrupting the route of transmission, and protecting the susceptible host.</p>
<p>There are various specific and general measures for protecting the host.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-measures">Specific Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immunisation using vaccines such as the KEPI vaccine</li>
<li>Chemoprophylaxis using for example:</li>
<li>Proguanil (PaludrineR) to suppress malaria parasites</li>
<li>Tetracycline during cholera outbreaks</li>
<li>Cotrimoxazole during plague outbreaks</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-measures">General Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use of barriers such as bed nets, gowns, gloves to prevent insect bites (especially mosquitoes)</li>
<li>Use of chemicals for example insect repellents to prevent mosquito bites</li>
<li>Wearing shoes to prevent penetration by hookworms from the soil</li>
<li>Adequate housing to reduce overcrowding</li>
<li>Improved nutrition</li>
<li>Adequate ventilation</li>
<li>Health education</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-control-measures">Other Control Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are other useful measures that can be taken to control the spread of communicable disease. Among these is the notification of disease. Notification requires you to keep watch (surveillance) on the number of new cases of communicable diseases in your area of work and to immediately inform the local health authority when you come across a patient suffering from an infectious disease. One of the main reasons for notification is to help the health authorities take measures to confirm your suspicion and to control the spread of the disease. Notification of infectious communicable diseases is the responsibility of all health care workers. It is also a legal requirement according to the Public Health Act, Chapter (cap) 242, section eight of the laws of Kenya.</p>
<p>Remember: It is your responsibility to notify your local health authority immediately should you suspect the presence of an infectious disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-any-six-notifiable-diseases-found-in-kenya">List any six notifiable diseases found in Kenya.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-any-six-notifiable-diseases-found-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="notifiable-diseases-in-kenya">Notifiable Diseases in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#notifiable-diseases-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Plague</li>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Measles</li>
<li>Poliomyelitis</li>
<li>Diphtheria</li>
<li>Tuberculosis</li>
<li>Anthrax</li>
<li>Trypanasomiasis</li>
<li>Typhoid fever</li>
<li>Whooping cough</li>
<li>Meningococcal meningitis</li>
<li>Rabies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="yellow-fever">Yellow fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#yellow-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The diseases in bold spread so quickly that they need international control measures. These diseases are reported by the Ministry of Health to the World Health Organisation (WHO).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="application-of-communicable-disease-control-measures">Application of Communicable Disease Control Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application-of-communicable-disease-control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The actual application of the control methods you have just seen can be undertaken by different groups of people and institutions at various levels. These include individuals and village level, dispensary and health centre level and the district and central government (Ministry of Health) level.</p>
<p>Remember: A successful communicable disease control program is the one that involves members of the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures-at-individual-and-village-level">Control Measures at Individual and Village Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures-at-individual-and-village-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At this level, each person and indeed every member of the village is responsible for:</p>
<ul>
<li>Completing the immunisation</li>
<li>Personal and environmental hygiene</li>
<li>Food hygiene and adequate nutrition</li>
<li>Using bed nets and protective wear</li>
<li>Abstaining from casual sex, being faithful to one sexual partner or using condoms</li>
<li>Protecting water supply and using clean water</li>
<li>Digging and using pit latrines</li>
<li>Controlling vectors</li>
<li>Healthy habits, for example not smoking, consuming alcohol and abuse of drugs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures-at-dispensary-and-health-centre-level">Control Measures at Dispensary and Health Centre Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures-at-dispensary-and-health-centre-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health care workers should support and encourage their clients and community to establish and sustain community based disease control programs. In addition, the health care workers should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increase immunisation coverage</li>
<li>Participate in vector and reservoir control</li>
<li>Emphasise water protection and purification</li>
<li>Inspect food, markets and eating places</li>
<li>Encourage sanitation and refuse disposal</li>
<li>Promote health and prevent diseases using Information, Education and Communication (IEC)</li>
<li>Notify diseases</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures-at-district-regional-and-national-level">Control Measures at District, Regional and National Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures-at-district-regional-and-national-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At these higher levels, health care workers are responsible for:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Vector control schemes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mass immunisation campaigns</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mass treatment and chemoprophylaxis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mass media IEC programmes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health statistics registration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Research on disease control methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Emergency, epidemiology and control teams</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Manpower training and continuing education for staff</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-contact-diseases">SECTION 3: CONTACT DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-contact-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Welcome to the third section of this unit. From this section onwards, you will group communicable diseases according to their mode of transmission and then investigate their individual causes, mode of transmission, diagnosis, treatment and preventive measures. You will start with contact diseases (also known as contagious diseases). This is a group of communicable diseases that are transmitted through direct or indirect contact between susceptible and infected persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>List factors that favour the transmission of contact (contagious) diseases</li>
<li>Identify signs and symptoms of infections, namely; scabies, fungal skin infections and trachoma</li>
<li>Describe the management of contagious diseases</li>
<li>Describe the control measures of contagious diseases</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="transmission-of-contact-diseases">Transmission of Contact Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-of-contact-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A large number of patients seen in your health facility, particularly school children, are suffering from contact diseases which are easily preventable. Contact diseases tend to occur in clusters within households, children's play groups, schools and workplaces. They are passed from one person to another either directly by skin-to-skin contact or indirectly by handling contaminated objects such as clothing,</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>bedding or combs. Such groups of infected people are known as clusters.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-3cceeb4a.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg">
Transmission of Contagious Diseases (Adapted from Communicable Diseases Manual, 1999. Transmission of Contagious Diseases.)</p>
<p>List four factors that increase the transmission of contact diseases.</p>
<p>Factors Increasing the Transmission of Contact Diseases.</p>
<ul>
<li>Close personal contact (for example: sexual intercourse)</li>
<li>Inadequate housing leading to overcrowding</li>
<li>Poor personal hygiene usually due to inadequate water supply</li>
<li>High population density as in urban (slums) areas</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scabies">Scabies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scabies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a parasitic infection of the superficial layer of the skin characterised by severe itching. It is caused by the female of an insect called Sarcoptes Scabiei (itch mite). The female mite burrows in to the skin and makes a small tunnel. Within the tunnel, the insect deposits its eggs and faeces. The eggs hatch in four to five days and the larvae leave the mother's tunnel and bury themselves in the skin and in other places. The larvae do not make tunnels.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Scabies is spread through direct close body contact, as in bed, or through contact between parents and children or among children playing together in schools. Transmission of scabies can also occur indirectly through clothing or bedclothes. Poor living conditions and poor hygiene promotes the spread of scabies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-picture">Clinical Picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient presents with intense itching, especially at night, and eczema-like signs. You will also find an itchy rash with typical distribution especially where the skin is curved (between fingers, elbows, buttocks, etc). Because it is very itchy, you might also find that the skin is torn with scratches and thus secondary infection often follows.</p>
<p>There are a number of reasons why people with scabies do not seek early medical attention. The skin lesions may be so common that they are not considered to be a disease. Also people who suffer from leprosy or other diseases which interfere with normal sensation may not feel the itching caused by scabies.</p>
<p><strong>Remember: Severe itching accompanied by typical distribution especially at the folds is suggestive of scabies</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The whole family should be treated together with the patient to prevent re-infection. The management of scabies is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient should take a warm bath.</li>
<li>Rub a handful of 10% Benzyl Benzoate Emulsion (BBE) all over the body.</li>
<li>After 24 hours, the patient should bathe again and put on clean clothes.</li>
<li>BBE does not kill the eggs of Sarcoptes Scabiei and therefore the treatment must be repeated after four to seven days to kill those larvae which have hatched since the first treatment.</li>
<li>If itching is severe treat it symptomatically with calamine lotion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-scabies">Prevention of Scabies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-scabies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The best way of preventing and treating scabies is good personal hygiene. Regular firm bathing, washing of clothes and frequent use of soap will control scabies.</p>
<p><strong>Remember: All these activities require regular supply of water.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dermatomycosis">Dermatomycosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dermatomycosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The term dermatomycosis means fungal infections of the skin and mucous membranes. Fungal skin infections are mainly a problem of personal appearance rather than illness, but it is important to distinguish them from leprosy and</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>syphilis. Also, fungal skin and mucous membrane infections are sometimes indicators of immunosuppression as occurs in AIDS, cancer and tuberculosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fungal infections are usually spread by direct and indirect contact. Genital infections such as vulvo-vaginitis may be spread during sexual intercourse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-picture">Clinical Picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A fungal infection typically produces a flat patch or shamba-like growth on the human skin. This patch may be found on the head, on dry exposed body skin, between the toes, or in moist places like the mouth or private parts. Each of these patches (depending on where they are found) looks slightly different and has a different name, but they are all fungi. Fungal infections can be divided into two groups: ringworms and candidiasis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ringworms">Ringworms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ringworms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ringworm manifestations are described in Latin after the areas of the body they commonly affect:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tinea capitis (ringworm of the scalp)</li>
<li>Tinea corporis (ringworm of the body)</li>
<li>Tinea pedis (ringworm of the foot)</li>
<li>Tinea unguium (ringworm of the nails)</li>
<li>Tinea versicolor or pityriasis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-ringworm-diseases">Characteristics of Ringworm Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-ringworm-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(Adapted from Communicable Diseases Manual, 1999, Characteristics of Fungal Skin Infections.)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Fungus</th><th>Risk Factors</th><th>Main Symptoms</th><th>Diagnosis</th><th>Treatment</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Tinea Capitis</td><td>Children under 10</td><td>Brittle hair; areas of broken hair on scalp</td><td></td><td>Whitefield's ointment b.i.d. for 3 weeks</td></tr><tr><td>Tinea corporis</td><td>Excessive sweating; hot and humid areas</td><td>Ring-shaped lesions; central healing</td><td>Branching filaments crossing borders of cells</td><td>Keep dry and clean</td></tr><tr><td>Tinea pedis (athlete's foot)</td><td>AIDS</td><td>Scaling and cracking of skin between toes</td><td></td><td>Apply Whitefield's ointment daily</td></tr><tr><td>Tinea unguium</td><td>Nail injuries; corticosteroids</td><td>Thickening, discoloration or brittleness of nails</td><td></td><td>Surgical removal of nails plus Whitefield's ointment daily for 16 weeks</td></tr><tr><td>Tinea versicolor</td><td>AIDS; excessive sweating; hot humid areas</td><td>Superficial small round light coloured areas</td><td>Short filaments, round thick walled cells, budding</td><td>Personal hygiene</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="candia-diasis">Candia diasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#candia-diasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Candia diasis which is also known as moniliasis or yeast infection manifests in the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>Oral thrush – patchy white dots which appear on the mucous membrane of the mouth</li>
<li>Vulvo-vaginitis</li>
<li>Balanitis</li>
<li>Intertrigo</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-candia-diasis-diseases">Characteristics of Candia diasis Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-candia-diasis-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(Adapted from Communicable Diseases Manual, 1999, Characteristics of Fungal Skin Infections.)</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trachoma">Trachoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trachoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a chronic inflammation of the conjunctiva and the cornea of the eye. It is caused by an organism called Chlamydia trachomatis of the Chlamydiae group. Other organisms of the Chlamydiae group cause non-gonococcal ophthalmia neonatorum, non-gonococcal urethritis, cervicitis and salpingitis. Trachoma is a major cause of blindness especially in those parts of East Africa where water is scarce, such as among the pastoralist communities who inhabit the drier grasslands.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trachoma is very common among communities living in dry areas where there is scarcity of water. Transmission of trachoma is by direct contact with the eye discharge of an infected person. Flies and fingers are important in the transmission of the disease. After infection, the disease progresses very slowly all the time destroying the cornea and the conjunctiva, eventually leading to permanent blindness in one or both eyes. The early stages of the diseases are the most infective and transmission is high among children.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-picture">Clinical Picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trachoma develops in four stages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-1-early-trachoma">Stage 1: Early Trachoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-1-early-trachoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Initially the eyes are red and watery (as in ordinary conjunctivitis). After 30 or more days, follicles (small pinkish-grey lumps) form inside the upper eyelids. To see these you would have to turn back the lid. Usually there is a little pus in the eye, but if the pus is copious this may indicate a secondary infection by bacteria. Examination of scrapings from the conjunctiva in the laboratory show the cells with a characteristic dark object in the cytoplasm. The dark object is called an inclusion body and its presence in the cell helps to confirm the diagnosis of trachoma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-2-pannus-formation">Stage 2: Pannus Formation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-2-pannus-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normally, the cornea has no blood capillaries on it. But during this stage, many tiny blood vessels are found to be growing towards the edge of the cornea. These tiny blood vessels which grow in the cornea are called pannus. You can see the pannus by using an ordinary magnifying glass. Again, the presence of both the follicles and the pannus strongly suggests the diagnosis of trachoma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-3-scarring-of-the-conjunctiva">Stage 3: Scarring of the Conjunctiva<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-3-scarring-of-the-conjunctiva" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After several years the follicles on the conjunctiva slowly begin to disappear leaving behind whitish scars on the conjunctiva. In the cornea, the small blood vessels degenerate. The vision becomes hazy and remains so for many years unless there is rupture of the cornea scars, in which case blindness occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-4-entropion-and-trichiasis-formation">Stage 4: Entropion and Trichiasis Formation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-4-entropion-and-trichiasis-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The scars formed after the healing process, several years after the onset of the disease, are the ones that do the greatest damage. Due to this scarring, the scar tissue retracts (shortens), thereby causing the eyelids</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 104 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>to become thick and to turn inwards. This is called entropion. As the thick, rough eyelids turn inwards, the eyelashes point inwards and rub against the cornea. This is called trichiasis. trichiasis adds to the damage already done to the eye and results in blindness</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember-the-combination-of-entropion-and-trichiasis-completely-destroy-the-cornea-leading-to-blindness">Remember: The combination of entropion and trichiasis completely destroy the cornea leading to blindness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember-the-combination-of-entropion-and-trichiasis-completely-destroy-the-cornea-leading-to-blindness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The drug of choice for the first three stages is 3% tetracycline topical eye ointment twice a day for five days every month for six months. Stage four of the disease with entropion must be treated surgically. It is essential to do this as soon as possible because every time the patient blinks it increases corneal damage. If it is not possible to perform surgery in your health facility, you can remove the in-turned eyelashes by pulling them out with sterile forceps. This should be done before you refer the patient. While entropion operations can be carried out at the health centre level, pannus and opacity of the cornea have to be done by eye specialists.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control-of-trachoma">Prevention and Control of Trachoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control-of-trachoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trachoma is an example of diseases that are associated with lack of water in the community (water scarcity). The most effective way of controlling and eradicating trachoma is through supply of adequate water to the community. Regular bathing and washing of children's faces with water and soap should be encouraged.</p>
<p>Other additional measures include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where water is scarce, the community should be taught how to use the 'leaky tin' (a technique where water for hand washing is put in a container that has a small hole near the bottom, the hole is closed with a piece of stick and when the sick is removed water trickles slowly. It minimises wastage of precious water in water scarce areas and improves personal hygiene) and be motivated to use it</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reducing the fly population in the community through proper disposal of refuse and waste</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early treatment of infected individuals</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mass treatment especially of school children who live in trachoma endemic areas using 3% tetracycline eye ointment twice a day for three to five days each month for six months</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-3d887367.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Prevention and Control of Trachoma</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-4-vector-borne-diseases">SECTION 4: VECTOR-BORNE DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-vector-borne-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this section you will examine communicable diseases which are transmitted by invertebrate hosts, that is organisms without a backbone. This section is longer than the previous one due to the large number of important diseases which fall under this group. As usual you will look at each type of disease, its causative organisms, clinical features, management and prevention.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>List at least nine common vector-borne diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the clinical features of vector-borne diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the transmission cycle of vector-borne diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the management of vector-borne diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discuss the preventive measures of vector-borne diseases namely:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malaria</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Filariasis</p>
</li>

<p>Yellowfever</p>
</li>

</li>

<p>Leishmaniasis</p>
</li>
