<p>This form of leishmaniasis occurs primarily in the tropics of South America. The disease begins with the same sores noted in localised cutaneous leishmaniasis. Sometimes these primary lesions heal, other times they spread and become larger. Some years after the first lesion is noted (and sometimes several years after that lesion has totally healed), new lesions appear in the mouth and nose, and occasionally in the area between the genitalia and the anus (the perineum). These new lesions are particularly destructive and painful. They erode underlying tissue and cartilage, frequently eating through the septum (the cartilage which separates the two nostrils). If the lesions spread to the roof of the mouth and the larynx (the part of the wind pipe which contains the vocal cords), they may prevent speech. Other symptoms include fever, weight loss, anaemia (low red blood cell count). There is always a large danger of bacteria infecting the already open sores.</p>
<p>Treatment is similar to that of cutaneous leishmaniasis. Prevention or early detection and appropriate treatment are preferred. Corrective surgery can be done where need arises.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Kala Azar can be prevented through:</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of insecticide treated curtains in homes (these have been used with success in Baringo district)</li>
<li>Destruction of infected dogs and rodents</li>
<li>Early diagnosis and treatment of the infected persons</li>
<li>Health education for communities on preventive measures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="plague">Plague<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plague" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a highly infectious disease caused by bacteria called yersinia pestis. Plague is a disease of rodents, especially rats and is spread from rat to rat by a rat flea called xenopsylla</p>
<p>cheopis. Plague is a very rare but serious disease because it can spread very rapidly unless the first case is recognised</p>
<p>early and appropriate action taken. It is also a serious disease with a high mortality rate (case fatality rate in the absence of treatment can be as high as 60%).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Plague occurs when infected wild rats, especially the sewer rat (R. norvegicus) die from the disease and their fleas look for substitute domestic rat (rattus italia) hosts. The domestic rat becomes infected and after it dies the fleas start biting human beings. When the first human is infected, the disease causes bubonic plague. People working in the fields may also be bitten by fleas from the dead infected wild rats and develop bubonic plague.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-a3d38add.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-picture">Clinical Picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Plague has three clinical presentations, bubonic, septicaemic and pneumonic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The diagnosis of plague can be confirmed by doing a microscopy (staining) of sputum or pus from the bubo to demonstrate the bacilli.</p>
<p>Remember: Early recognition of plague followed by correct action is a matter of life or death.</p>
<p>You must start treatment as soon as you confirm the diagnosis from clinical and laboratory findings. The plague bacillus (Yersinia pestis) is sensitive to most common antibiotics except penicillin. Drug treatment with any of the following antibiotics is effective:</p>
<ul>
<li>IM streptomycin 30mg/kg two to four times daily for ten days</li>
<li>Oral or IV tetracycline 10mg/kg six hourly for ten days</li>
<li>Oral cotrimoxazole two tabs twelve hourly for seven days</li>
<li>Oral chloramphenicol 500mg six hourly for seven days</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember: Plague is an internationally notifiable disease.</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>Prevention and Control</p>
<p>The prevention and control of plague depends on the following measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>Early diagnosis and notification so that the patients are not moved or referred to the hospital</li>
<li>Chemoprophylaxis of all contacts of the patients such as family, visitors and health care workers using tetracycline or cotrimoxazole</li>
<li>Isolation of the infected and quarantine of the contacts for ten days</li>
<li>Use of insecticides to kill fleas</li>
<li>Eradication of rats, for example using rat poison</li>
<li>Vaccination during epidemics using an anti-plague vaccine</li>
<li>Health education for communities on preventive measures</li>
</ul>
<p>Relapsing Fever</p>
<p>This is an acute infectious bacterial disease which is characterised by alternating febrile periods. It is also known as Recurrent fever, Spirillum, Tick fever, or Tick Bite fever. It is transmitted by ticks and lice. There are two types of relapsing fever, namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Louse-borne relapsing fever</li>
<li>Tick-borne relapsing fever</li>
</ul>
<p>The louse-borne relapsing fever is spread by the human head louse, pediculus capitis, and the body louse, pediculus corporis. They transmit spirochaetes of the genus borrelia reccurentis. The tick-borne relapsing fever is transmitted by soft ticks (ornithodoros moubata) which live in cracks and crevices of walls and floors. They transmit spirochaetes of the genus borrelia duttoni, which cause tick-borne relapsing fever. Children, visitors and pregnant women travelling to endemic areas are more susceptible to the disease. Adults in endemic areas are semi-immune to relapsing fever.</p>
<p>Mode of Transmission</p>
<p>The disease is transmitted from person to person by the bite of the head louse, body louse or soft tick.</p>
<p>Louse-borne</p>
<p>The human louse transmits louse-borne relapsing fever from person to person. When the louse feeds on the blood of an infected person, it takes up the bacteria. The bacteria multiply within the body of the louse (but these spirochaetes are not found in the saliva or the excreta of the louse). The infection is transmitted to another person only when the louse is crushed on the body surface near a bite wound. The offspring of an infected louse does not carry the spirochaetes. Epidemics of louse-borne relapsing fever are associated with times of war and famine when refugees are crowded together in unsanitary conditions, which promote infestation with human body lice.</p>
<p>Tick-borne</p>
<p>Tick-borne relapsing fever is transmitted when a tick sucks blood from an infected person. The spirochaetes are taken up and multiply in the tick's body. In seven days, the spirochaetes appear in the tick's salivary glands and the coxal fluid ready to be transmitted to a new host. The organisms can either be injected directly when the tick feeds on the host, or they can infect a new host by penetrating intact mucous membranes (for example in laboratory infections).</p>
<p>Unlike in louse-borne fever where the offspring does not carry the organism, in tick-borne fever the borrelia duttoni organisms pass into the ovary of the tick, thus automatically infecting the offspring of the ticks (vertical transmission). In</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>this way, a house once inhabited by infected ticks will remain dangerous for up to ten years. In an infected pregnant woman, the spirochaete can cross the placenta to the foetus resulting either in abortion, stillbirth, premature delivery, or congenital infection in the newborn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient presents with sudden onset of fever which ranges between 39.5°C - 40.5°C. There is rapid pulse, headache, aching joints, vomiting and infected conjunctiva. Often there is potential rash, epistaxis, and herpes labialis. After five to seven days, the temperature drops by crisis. In about 60% of the patients, a less severe relapse of the symptoms occurs five to ten days after the first attack. A second relapse may occur in about 25% of the patients. In untreated cases, there may be up to ten relapses. The fever and clinical symptoms become less severe each time after the relapse. Relapsing fever has a high mortality rate of 40%. Common complications of relapsing fever include meningitis, iritis, optic nerve atrophy (blindness), myocarditis and liver failure bleeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You can confirm relapsing fever by doing a microscopic examination of a thick blood smear for the spirochaetes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treatment should eradicate the spirochaete from the body without eliciting Jarisch-Herxheimer reaction. Some deaths occur after starting treatment as a result of a severe Jarisch-Herxheimer reaction. The antibiotics suddenly kill a large number of spirochaetes which release toxins into the circulation causing the patient to collapse. This reaction is characterised by chills, rapid breathing, elevated temperature (40 - 42°C), confusion, delirium, and sometimes convulsions and coma. The patient then develops very severe hypotension, and may go into heart failure. This complication is however not seen in tick-borne infections. Patients must be nursed flat, given adequate fluids and be confined to bed for at least 24 hours.</p>
<p>The treatment of relapsing fever is IM procaine penicillin 400,000 units stat, followed the next day by oral tetracycline 500mg six hourly for five to seven days. An alternative to tetracycline is oral doxycycline 200mg once (single dose).</p>
<p>Remember: Tetracycline should not be given to children and pregnant women because it discolours the teeth permanently and also causes premature calcification of bones.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="louse-borne">Louse-borne<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#louse-borne" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>To eradicate lice you should advise the patient to do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improve their personal hygiene</li>
<li>Use insecticides to kill lice, for example malathion powder</li>
<li>Boil clothes to kill lice and eggs (delousing)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="onchocerciasis">Onchocerciasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#onchocerciasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Onchocerciasis is a chronic disease caused by a filarial worm called onchocerca volvulus. It lives in the subcutaneous and connective tissue of the infected person. It manifests mainly as skin nodules on bony surfaces, and causes eye lesions which result in blindness. That is why it is also known as river blindness. The vector for O. volvulus is the female black fly of the genus simulium. In western African countries where the disease is more prevalent, the vector is simulium damnosum, while in East Africa the vector is simulium neavei. The disease is found in western Uganda, southern Sudan, and eastern Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC). Blackflies are able to travel up to 80km in a day. The simulium fly breeds in fast running well aerated rivers or turbulent areas of a river such as at the waterfalls and rapids. The eggs of the simulium fly are able to develop into larvae only in water that is rich in oxygen, such as fast flowing rivers. Larvae are attached to submerged plants, rocks and living crabs. The female O. volvulus worm is only about 0.3mm in diameter but can be as long as half a meter (50cm) long. The male is about 0.2mm in diameter and 4 - 13cm long.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>River blindness is spread from person to person by the bite of an infected blackfly. Black flies feed during the day both inside and outside</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>houses. They usually bite early in the morning or late in the evening.</p>
<p>The blackfly takes up microfilariae when it sucks the blood of an infected person. Once in the stomach, the microfilariae penetrate the stomach wall and travel to the thoracic muscles where they develop further for about seven days. They then move to the head of the fly ready to be transmitted to the next susceptible person when the fly feeds.</p>
<p>When the fly bites again, it injects the larvae of O. volvulus into the skin of the healthy host. The larvae mature in the human subcutaneous tissue into adult worms in about one to three years.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-231835c9.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After the adult O. volvulus has lived in the body of an infected person for about one year, it begins to give birth to microfilariae. One adult female worm can produce up to one million microfilariae every year. The microfilariae of O.volvulus have a strong liking for the skin and eyes of the infected host. Adult worms live up to 17 years in nodules in the subcutaneous and connective tissue. Most nodules are found on the bony skin surface such as the elbow, skull, ribs, iliac, crests, and shoulder scapula. The disease has four different clinical presentations:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="severe-itching">Severe Itching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#severe-itching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is one of the early symptoms and mainly affects the buttocks. The severe itching is often accompanied by skin depigmentation giving rise to a 'leopard skin'.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skin-nodules">Skin Nodules<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin-nodules" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are caused by the adult worms which you saw earlier like to live in the skin. They contain adult worms and are painless, rubbery, and firm; ranging in diameter from 3mm - 3cm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dermatitis">Dermatitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dermatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is caused by a reaction to the presence of microfilariae in the epidermis and manifests as itchy papules and macules. Later, the skin becomes loose, scaly, atrophic and depigmented.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blindness">Blindness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blindness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is caused by the presence of microfilariae in the cornea and the anterior chamber of the eye. It starts with oedema of conjunctiva; then corneal spots and a pannus begin to develop. Finally cataracts, iritis, sclerosing keratitis, and glaucoma develop leading to blindness. You can differentiate between trachoma and river blindness because in river blindness the pannus start at the lower limbus, while in trachoma it affects the upper limbus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The diagnosis is made by examining skin snips from the thighs, buttocks and iliac crests under a microscope for microfilariae.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Onchocerciasis is not a fatal disease. If the patient has no serious complaints and is likely to be re-infected, there is no urgency for treatment, since the traditional drugs used have been known to cause severe reactions. However, the following groups of patients do need treatment:</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient with eye lesions</li>
<li>Patients with severe skin lesions</li>
<li>Patients with heavy infections</li>
</ul>
<p>Two types of treatment are used in the management of this disease. The first one is to kill the microfilariae. Give the patient oral Ivermectine (mectizan) 150 microgram/kg single dose repeated once every six to twelve months. The second type of treatment is aimed at killing or removing the adult worms by surgical resection of the nodules.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following measures have been found to be useful in preventing onchocerciasis:</p>
<ul>
<li>Addition of insecticide to the water of rivers known to be breeding places of the simulium fly</li>
<li>Wearing of long clothing which covers most of the body</li>
<li>Moving the whole community away from sites near where black flies breed</li>
<li>Treating infected people with microfilaricides</li>
<li>Mass treatment of communities using ivermectine</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 121 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-5-diseases-caused-by-faecal-oral-contamination">SECTION 5: DISEASES CAUSED BY FAECAL-ORAL CONTAMINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-5-diseases-caused-by-faecal-oral-contamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diseases caused by faecal-oral contamination are those whose causative organisms are excreted in the stool of an infected person and then, by various ways, enter the mouth of a susceptible person.</p>
<p>Water that looks clean to the eye may be dangerously polluted. Contaminated food may look, smell and taste delicious and yet harbour dangerous organisms. Food and water transmits diseases if contaminated by infected hands, soil, flies, animals, animal products or polluted water. Flies transmit diseases by vomiting on food or by carrying pathogens from faeces and transferring them to food. Indeed, most of the primary diarrhoeal diseases are caused by direct contamination of food or water by faeces, through flies and fingers.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-4435d965.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>List eight common diseases spread by the faecal-oral route</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the methods used to interrupt the transmission cycle of faecal-oral transmitted diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the clinical features, of faecal-oral route transmitted diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the management of faecal-oral route transmitted diseases.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Now move on to look at the diseases one by one starting with enteric fevers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="enteric-fevers">Enteric Fevers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enteric-fevers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Enteric fevers include typhoid fever and paratyphoid A and B fevers. Typhoid fever is an infectious disease characterised by high continuous fever, malaise and involvement of lymphoid tissue and spleen. Diarrhoea is not a common symptom in typhoid fever.</p>
<p>Paratyphoid fever may present like typhoid fever, but in most cases it presents as gastroenteritis or transient diarrhoea. Both are mainly spread by the faecal-oral route through contaminated food, water and milk. Flies are also important in the transmission of enteric fevers.</p>
<p>You will now consider each type of disease in turn.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-afb244f5.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="typhoid-fever">Typhoid Fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#typhoid-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an infectious bacterial disease caused by salmonella typhi.</p>
<p>Typhoid fever is endemic in many regions of East Africa, although epidemic outbreaks have occurred when a source of water or food used by many people has been contaminated.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 122 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The disease has a case fatality rate of 3% with treatment and 10% without adequate antibiotic treatment. Human beings are the only known reservoir and host.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incubation period of typhoid fever is 7 - 21 days. The disease has a gradual onset which progresses through the following four stages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-week">First Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the first week and early in the disease, the patient has severe headache, malaise, loss of appetite, body pains and aches and a tendency to nose-bleed.</p>
<p>The body temperature rises day by day or in steps to 39.5°C or higher. Most patients cough because they develop bronchitis and may also complain of constipation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-week">Second Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the second week, temperature continues to rise, but the pulse rate is slower than would be expected for that temperature. There is swelling of lymphoid tissue in the intestines as well as Peyer's patches, necrosis and ulcers, which cause the abdomen to become distended and tender.</p>
<p>The high temperature and toxaemia causes mental confusion and disorientation in the patient. Half the patients may develop greenish watery ('pea-soup') diarrhoea and bronchopneumonia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="third-week">Third Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Body temperature decreases step by step and the patient improves slowly. If there is no improvement, the Peyer's patches in the intestines perforate and toxaemia increases.</p>
<p>The patient becomes delirious and incontinent of urine and stool, muscles twitch and coma may precede death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fourth-week">Fourth Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fourth-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For the patients who do not suffer the serious complications of the third week, the fourth week is a period of convalescence.</p>
<p>The temperature drops back to normal and the patient recovers gradually.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The best way to diagnose typhoid fever is through a blood culture. This may be positive during the first week and for a variable period after this. Stool and urine cultures can also be made although they are only positive after the first week. Other tests which are undertaken include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Widal test during the first and second week, that is indicative of high and rising titres</li>
<li>WBC count which indicates low levels (leucopenia) with raised lymphocyte count</li>
<li>Stool to check for presence of occult blood which is found in 100% of the cases</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-reliable-is-the-widal-test-in-typhoid-diagnosis">How reliable is the Widal test in typhoid diagnosis?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-reliable-is-the-widal-test-in-typhoid-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although the Widal test is still very useful, especially when two tests are performed four to five days apart after the end of the first week, its interpretation is full of difficulties especially in endemic areas and in people who have had the typhoid vaccine. That is why it is a good idea to also carry out one of the other laboratory tests.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The treatment of typhoid fever includes the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fluid replacement due to diarrhoea</li>
<li>Oral norfloxacin 400mg 12 hourly for 10 - 14 days</li>
<li>Oral ciproxacin 500mg bd. for 14 days</li>
<li>Oral corticosteroids to prevent Jarisch-Herxheimer's reaction</li>
<li>Patient should be isolated in fly-proof room</li>
<li>Contaminated articles should be disposed by incineration</li>
<li>Stools and urine should be disposed of in a pit latrine or septic tank</li>
<li>Surgical treatment for perforated bowels</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong></p>
<p>When treatment is started early it is not usually necessary to refer typhoid patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The prevention and control of typhoid fever is similar to that of many diarrhoea diseases. It includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Identification of the carriers especially those who work as food handlers and treat them promptly</li>
<li>Administration of typhoid vaccine</li>
<li>Safe water supply</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Improvement in food hygiene</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paratyphoid-fever">Paratyphoid Fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paratyphoid-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the second type of enteric fever which was mentioned earlier. It is caused by bacteria known as salmonella paratyphi types A, B and C. The disease runs a milder course than typhoid fever and also has enlargement of the spleen, bloodstained diarrhoea and swelling of the Peyer's patches.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The treatment of paratyphoid fever is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Intravenous fluid if diarrhoea is severe</li>
<li>Oral rehydration if diarrhoea is mild</li>
<li>Oral contrimoxazole two tablets bd. for five to seven days</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The prevention and control measures are similar to those that were covered under typhoid fever.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cholera">Cholera<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cholera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cholera is an intestinal disease which is characterised by sudden onset of profuse watery stools and vomiting, leading to severe dehydration, acidosis and circulatory collapse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidemiology-of-cholera">Epidemiology of Cholera<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology-of-cholera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is caused by a small comma-shaped motile organism called vibrio cholerae. There are about four sub-strains of the cholera vibrio, namely, El Tor, Ogawa, Luaba and Hikojima. The El Tor sub-strain causes cholera epidemics in East Africa.</p>
<p>Cholera is transmitted through the faecal-oral route, mostly by water which has been contaminated with faecal matter. The vibrios are very sensitive to the hydrochloric acid found in the human stomach, and so a large number of organisms must be ingested for infection to occur.</p>
<p>Cholera occurs in all parts of the world where the living conditions are unsanitary.</p>
<p>The human being is the reservoir and host. Vibrios prefer brackish (salty) water. In seawater, the organisms can live even longer multiplying in crabs and shrimps. Vibrios also multiply in certain foods such as milk and boiled rice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-the-role-and-importance-of-carriers">What is the role and importance of carriers?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-the-role-and-importance-of-carriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The reservoir of infection in cholera is formed mainly by the carriers. For every clinical case of cholera there may be 50 - 100 asymptomatic carriers. Although the carriers excrete a smaller number of vibrios than the patients, they form the greatest danger to the community because of their sheer number and freedom of movement.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-b044d8d4.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cholera has a short incubation period of two to three days. The vibrios remain in the digestive tract from where they cause water loss and electrolyte imbalance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-signs-and-symptoms-would-lead-you-to-suspect-cholera">What signs and symptoms would lead you to suspect cholera?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-signs-and-symptoms-would-lead-you-to-suspect-cholera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unlike typhoid, cholera is not a systemic infection and therefore fever is generally low or absent. Cholera progresses through the following three stages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-stage">First Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This stage lasts for 3 - 12 hours. During this stage profuse watery stool is passed by the patient until faecal matter disappears. The stool becomes almost clear fluid with flakes of mucus, giving it the classical rice-water stool appearance. Vomiting follows diarrhoea. Initially the patient vomits food but soon after only clear fluid or rice-water is vomited. The patient develops severe cramps in the abdomen and limbs due to electrolyte loss.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-stage">Second Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient becomes severely dehydrated, the skin is cold, dry and inelastic. Blood pressure drops severely, and it may not be recordable. The pulse becomes weak and rapid, urine</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>production ceases, patient collapses and may go into irreversible shock.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="third-stage">Third Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the stage of recovery. Some patients recover spontaneously or with treatment. The general condition rapidly improves, diarrhoea becomes less profuse and the patient is able to take oral fluids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cholera should be suspected in any outbreak of diarrhoeal diseases. The diagnosis is made on clinical grounds and also through laboratory isolation of vibrio cholerae from a rectal swab, stool or vomitus specimen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of cholera is easily done at health centre level and so there is no need to refer patients to hospital. This is because the main cause of death in cholera patients is dehydration. This can occur very quickly and early in an outbreak before the urgency of treatment is recognised. Therefore early rehydration is the most important part of management.</p>
<p>Other measures taken in the management of cholera include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The immediate notification of district medical officer. Cholera is an internationally notifiable disease.</li>
<li>Admission of patients in temporary treatment centres, such as school or church and the treatment of patients on 'cholera beds', that is beds with a central hole through which the stools can pass into a bucket and measured.</li>
<li>Barrier nursing and patient isolation should be practiced to prevent spread of the disease.</li>
<li>Disinfection of hospital equipment and proper disposal of stool and vomitus into a pit latrine or septic tanks.</li>
</ul>
<p>Now move on to see more measures that are taken in the management of cholera.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-3bf00cb3.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<p>Measures taken in the management of cholera also include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immediate introduction of intravenous fluids to correct the severe fluid and electrolyte loss. If this is started in time it can save many cholera cases. As soon as a patient is able to drink, Oral Rehydration Solution (ORS) should be given in water at a rate of 200 - 300ml per hour.</li>
<li>Intravenous fluids for patients who are in shock or too weak to drink.</li>
<li>Oral tetracycline, 500mg six hourly for five days. This speeds up recovery and prevents convalescent carrier state.</li>
<li>Oral cotrimoxazole, two tablets 12 hourly for three days can also be used effectively.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rehydration will save almost all cholera cases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following measures are useful in the prevention and control of cholera.</p>
<ul>
<li>Surveillance: early detection is central to the success of cholera control because it enables immediate action to be taken as soon as there is an outbreak of the disease. Surveillance leads to immediate notification of an outbreak.</li>
<li>Provision of clean safe water to the community can easily control cholera because it is mainly a water borne disease.</li>
<li>Teaching and demonstrating to members of the community cheap and effective methods of purifying water at their home.</li>
<li>Foods which can transmit cholera such as milk, should be pasteurised or boiled; raw or uncooked food should be avoided or washed in safe water, foods</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 125 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>should be protected from flies and markets inspected.</p>
<p>Now move on to see more measures that are useful in the prevention and control of cholera.</p>
<p>Measures that are useful in the prevention and control of cholera also include.</p>
<ul>
<li>Encouraging the digging and use of pit latrines.</li>
<li>Provision of chemoprophylaxis to all contacts of the patients including family, friends and visitors using oral tetracycline.</li>
<li>Administering cholera vaccine to health care workers in contact with the patients during the epidemics.</li>
<li>Enrolling the assistance of formal and informal community leaders to address negative cultures and customs that contribute to the spread of cholera. Such communities should be targeted with information, education and communication messages.</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember:
Cholera is an internationally notifiable disease.</p>
<p>Bacillary Dysentery (Shigellosis)</p>
<p>Bacillary dysentery, also known as shigellosis, is an acute bacterial disease of the intestines. It is common especially in areas where the standards of hygiene are low, particularly, where there is scarcity of safe water, improper human excreta disposal, large population of flies and child malnutrition. Once again humans are the only known reservoir.</p>
<p>It is caused by a non-motile gram-negative bacilli of the genus shigella spp. The organisms responsible for outbreaks are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Shigella sonnei</li>
<li>Shigella dysenteriae</li>
<li>Shigella flexneri</li>
<li>Shigella boydii</li>
</ul>
<p>However, the first three organisms are the most common causes of outbreaks.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-366b7039.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<p>Mode of Transmission</p>
<p>The mode of transmission of the disease is the faecal-oral route. The organisms are transmitted directly through flies or contaminated hands.</p>
<p>Indirect transmission may also occur through dishes which are poorly washed. The shigella multiply in food which when ingested causes dysentery.</p>
<p>Clinical Features</p>
<p>The disease has a short incubation period of one to four days. The onset is sudden with fever, headache, diarrhoea with streaks of blood, and colicky abdominal pains.</p>
<p>After a few motions (usually in a few hours) diarrhoea stops and is followed by severe colicky abdominal pain known as dysenteric syndrome, and painful contractions of the sphincter ani which produce an irresistible urge to defecate (tenesmus). When the patient goes to the toilet they pass small amounts of purulent mucus and blood. Vomiting may also occur. Toxins produced by the shigella on the wall of the colon may be absorbed into the blood stream resulting in toxaemia. Toxaemia causes high fever and rapid pulse. Dehydration is also common and dangerous as it may cause muscular cramps, oliguria and shock. In infants, rectal prolapse may occur as well as convulsions.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-0b5b651a.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg">
The 4 F Connection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following laboratory examinations are undertaken:</p>
<ul>
<li>Stool examination which shows the presence of blood and mucus</li>
<li>Stool microscopy which shows presence of large numbers of white blood cells and erythrocytes</li>
<li>Stool culture for shigella spp.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mild bacillary dysentery is self-limiting and all it requires is prevention or treatment of dehydration. However, in the case of severe infection, you will need to combine rehydration with antibiotics as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antibiotics: oral ciprofloxacin 500mg 12 hourly for five to seven days</li>
<li>Analgesics for colic such as codeine phosphate and loperamide, belladonna, or paracetamol</li>
<li>Rehydration due to diarrhoea and fluid loss. Oral rehydration using ORS in water is always useful as an aid to parenteral rehydration. It also carries less danger of disturbing electrolyte balance. However, intravenous fluid should be given to the very ill who cannot take anything orally.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The prevention and control of bacillary dysentery depends on stopping the faecal-oral transmission through the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Safe water supply</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improvement in personal hygiene</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Digging and use of pit latrines</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Practising food hygiene</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Giving health education that emphasises environmental hygiene and breastfeeding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inspection of public eating places, markets, boarding schools and camps</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="giardiasis">Giardiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#giardiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an infection of the small intestines by protozoa called giardia lamblia. The disease may be mild (asymptomatic) in some individuals, while in others it may cause diarrhoea, malabsorption of digested nutrients and weight loss.</p>
<p>Giardiasis is found in all the countries of the world, but it is more common in developing countries such as Kenya, where the water supply may be contaminated by human faeces or sewerage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Often, the disease is spread from person to person, especially within families by asymptomatic carriers.</p>
<p>Cysts which are excreted in the stool of an infected person remain infectious for up to three months in cold water or four days if the temperature is 37°C. As soon as the cysts are ingested by a human being, they are activated by the hydrochloric acid in the stomach. Trophozoites emerge and adhere to the wall of the upper portion of the small intestine. Here they begin to multiply and in about 10 - 14 days, the symptoms manifest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acute giardiasis is characterised by sudden onset of nausea, loss of appetite, abdominal distension (bloating sensation), prominent bowel sounds, and diarrhoea with frequent, frothy, yellowish stools with offensive odour. Fatigue, lethargy and weight loss often occur.</p>
<p>After about three weeks the symptoms reduce in severity and for many of the patients, this is the beginning of spontaneous recovery. Some patients however, remain symptomatic and continue to lose weight because of ongoing malabsorption of nutrients, mostly fat, vitamin B12 and lactose. The disease may persist for months or years</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diagnosis of giardiasis is often difficult to establish because stool examination rarely</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 127 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>reveals motile trophozoites. However, approximately 60% of samples will show cysts. The diagnosis is therefore made through the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>Stool microscopy to show cysts (three separate stool specimens should be collected to increase sensitivity of the test)</li>
<li>Serology (giardia antigens can be detected in stools) - immunological test</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any one of the following three alternative treatments is effective enough to clear the infection:</p>
<ul>
<li>Oral tinidazole 50mg/kg body weight single dose</li>
<li>Oral metronidazole 2g single dose. Repeat the dose after ten days to increase the cure rate</li>
<li>Oral metronidazole 250mg eight hourly for seven days</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cysts of giardia lamblia are not affected by chlorine treatment of water or by iodine. However, they are highly susceptible to heat, therefore, the following preventive measures are important:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cooking food and boiling drinking water to kill the cysts</li>
<li>Advise people to avoid eating raw salads, ice cream, unpeeled fruit and ice cubes in endemic areas</li>
<li>Use of sand filters is also effective in protecting water from giardia cysts</li>
<li>Tracing and treatment of healthy human carriers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="amoebiasis">Amoebiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amoebiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a protozoal infection mainly of the intestinal mucous membrane in humans caused by entamoeba histolytica. The disease is found in all parts of the world but more common where sanitary conditions are poor. Amoebiasis can occur in families or spread through institutions but usually does not occur in epidemics. It can be endemic in a population in which many individuals are asymptomatic cyst-passers with only a few getting the disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cysts are passed from person to person by the faecal-oral route, by fingers soiled with faeces either directly into the mouth or via food. Infections may also occur from drinking contaminated water. Amoebiasis can occasionally spread from the bowels to other organs of the body, especially to the liver leading to amoebic liver disease.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-bb4def28.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathogenesis">Pathogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the cysts are ingested, the emerging trophozoites take up residence in the intestinal mucosa.</p>
<p>The organisms multiply in the mucosa (causing the formation of bottle-shaped ulcers each 1-2cm in diameter). Too many such ulcers may cover the large intestine. Some of the ulcers may become perforated leading to severe peritonitis with shock. In the small intestines, the entamoeba histolytica may pass through the mucous membrane and enter the liver. After a variable incubation period a liver abscess may form.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The signs and symptoms of amoebiasis include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Colicky abdominal pain</li>
<li>Watery foul smelling diarrhoea containing blood-streaked mucus</li>
<li>There may be a hard large tender abdominal mass (amoebic)</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 128 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Remember:
Amoebic infection is usually asymptomatic.</p>
<p>Diagnosis
This is reached by doing a stool microscopy for cysts of entamoeba histolytica.</p>
<p>Management
No treatment is necessary for asymptomatic patients as in time they clear the infection. However, for invasive disease either one of the following treatments is effective:</p>
<ul>
<li>Oral metronidazole 800mg eight hourly for five to seven days</li>
<li>Oral diloxamide furoate 500mg eight hourly for ten days</li>
</ul>
<p>In hepatic amoebiasis, oral metronidazole is very effective.
A three day course of 1.4g - 2.4g a day will treat the disease.</p>
<p>Extra-intestinal Amoebic Disease
The most common site for extra-intestinal amoebiasis is the liver where it forms a liver abscess. Other secondary sites include lungs and skin leading to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Amoebic infection of the skin</li>
<li>Amoebic balanitis</li>
<li>Amoebic lung abscess</li>
<li>Amoebic brain abscess</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention and Control</p>
<p>Who is responsible for the spread of amoebic dysentery?
It is the cysts-passers who are usually asymptomatic. Therefore in order to prevent and control this disease, you need to do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise people to boil drinking water (chlorination does not kill the cysts)</li>
<li>Search for and treat carriers among food handlers</li>
<li>Commence a campaign for more latrines in an area with endemic amoebiasis</li>
<li>Conduct community campaigns about good personal hygiene practices, such as regular hand washing</li>
</ul>
<p>Viral Hepatitis
This is an acute viral disease which mainly affects the liver, causing inflammation of the liver cells (hepatocellular inflammation) followed by jaundice. The disease is found in all the countries of the world. There are five types of viruses which cause hepatitis. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hepatitis A Virus (HAV)</li>
<li>Hepatitis B Virus (HBV)</li>
<li>Hepatitis C Virus (HCV)</li>
<li>Hepatitis D Virus (HDV)</li>
<li>Hepatitis E Virus (HEV)</li>
</ul>
<p>Hepatitis A virus causes infectious hepatitis and is the most infectious of these viruses, while hepatitis B virus causes serum hepatitis (also called epidemic hepatitis). The hepatitis B virus causes chronic active infection of the liver (hepatitis) which may be followed some ten years later by liver cirrhosis (in 10 - 20% of the patients). In some of the patients who develop cirrhosis, the disease progresses to liver cancer (hepatocellular carcinoma). Hepatitis B infection occurs in about 1 - 3% of the human beings, but the incidence may be higher in patients undergoing kidney dialysis and in cancer wards (due to repeated blood transfusions), and among children because of close personal contact. It is difficult to tell the difference between infectious hepatitis and serum hepatitis on clinical observations alone.</p>
<p>Mode of Transmission
Hepatitis A and E infections are transmitted through faecal-oral route and are both called infectious hepatitis. Hepatitis B, C and D are transmitted through blood products and close personal contacts and are called serum hepatitis. Serum hepatitis may cause chronic liver infection and liver cirrhosis.</p>
<p>The human being is the only known reservoir and host of viral hepatitis. The disease is transmitted from the infected person to the susceptible host through faeces, contaminated food and objects, blood, blood serum and other body fluids.</p>
<p>In the case of hepatitis B infection, transmission takes place through two main routes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Percutaneous route - this is through injections and transfusion of blood and blood products.</li>
<li>Non-percutaneous routes - these include close personal contact for example, kissing and sexual intercourse, from mother to foetus</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 129 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
