<p>through placenta or to baby during delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All types of hepatitis infections are characterised by a similar clinical picture. The incubation period is one to four weeks in the case of hepatitis A and 12 weeks or longer in the case of hepatitis B. Hepatitis infections manifest in two phases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-icteric-phase-no-jaundice">Pre-icteric Phase (no jaundice)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-icteric-phase-no-jaundice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fever of sudden onset</li>
<li>Malaise</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
<li>Abdominal discomfort</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="icteric-phase">Icteric Phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#icteric-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Appearance of jaundice</li>
<li>Enlarged tender liver (hepatomegaly)</li>
<li>Extreme tiredness and myalgia</li>
<li>Feelings of deep sadness (depression)</li>
<li>Pale stools</li>
<li>Dark urine (contains bilirubin)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="those-at-risk-of-hepatitis">Those At Risk of Hepatitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#those-at-risk-of-hepatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reservoirs of hepatitis B virus include sexually promiscuous individuals, spouses of acutely infected persons, health care workers exposed to blood, family members of chronically infected persons, anyone who requires repeated blood transfusions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="how-would-you-diagnose-viral-hepatitis-in-a-patient">How would you diagnose viral hepatitis in a patient?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-would-you-diagnose-viral-hepatitis-in-a-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The urine of a person suffering from viral hepatitis is dark and contains bilirubin, while the stool is usually pale. In the blood, both direct and indirect bilirubin levels are raised. In the case of hepatitis B, diagnosis is made by detecting various immunological markers in the blood. The most important is the hepatitis B surface antigen (HBsAg) which is present when the virus is in the blood in the acute stage and in the chronic carrier state.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>No specific treatment is available for both hepatitis A and B.</p>
<p>The patient should be given symptomatic treatment together with diet and bed rest at home to prevent the spread of the disease. If admission is indicated for one reason or the other, you should ensure that the patient is isolated and extra precautions taken during handling and disposal of excreta. Since alcohol increases the risk of cirrhosis, you should advise the patient to avoid alcohol for at least six months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Just like in the other diseases that have been covered, improvement of environmental sanitation will prevent the transmission of hepatitis A.</p>
<p>Other control measures include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Isolating patients suffering viral hepatitis</li>
<li>Administration of hepatitis vaccine</li>
<li>Screening blood for hepatitis B surface antigen before giving it for transfusion and excluding all donors with a history of jaundice</li>
<li>Effective sterilisation and high level disinfection of all instruments, needles and syringes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bacterial-food-poisoning">Bacterial Food Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bacterial-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Food poisoning is a sudden, acute and sometimes life threatening illness which follows ingestion of contaminated food, drink or water. The major causes of food poisoning include intoxication with chemicals, toxins produced by bacterial growth, and a variety of organic substances such as poisonous plants and mushrooms. Food poisoning occurs in small outbreaks and mortality is usually low. In this country, you often hear of severe cases of food poisoning caused by consumption of cheap alcoholic drinks ('Kumi Kumi'). It is also suspected that some cases diagnosed as gastroenteritis in health facilities are actually caused by food poisoning.</p>
<p>There are two common types of bacterial food poisoning found in communities.</p>
<p>These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Staphylococcal food poisoning</li>
<li>Clostridium botulinum food poisoning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staphylococcal-food-poisoning">Staphylococcal Food Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staphylococcal-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of poisoning is caused by contamination of food (for example, with pus</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>from a septic finger) by an infected person). The staphylococci in the pus multiply and produce toxins when the food is allowed to stand for several hours before being served. Although the bacteria itself is harmless if ingested, the toxins it produces are very poisonous. Following ingestion of the toxin-contaminated food, there is sudden severe abdominal cramping, nausea, vomiting, diarrhoea, headache and excessive salivation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This disease is usually recognised when people who have shared food all fall sick within a short time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clostridium-botulinum-food-poisoning">Clostridium Botulinum Food Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clostridium-botulinum-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Botulinum poisoning occurs when food contaminated with botulinum spores (from the soil) is kept warm and in tightly covered containers for many hours. The organisms multiply in warm anaerobic (low oxygen) environments especially in protein-rich foods.</p>
<p>When such food is contaminated, clostridium botulinum multiplies and starts producing toxins. The contaminated food may appear spoiled (greenish) and emit an offensive odour. Once a person eats this food, they may suffer a mild illness that requires no medical treatment or a rapidly fatal illness terminating in death within 24 hours.</p>
<p>The symptoms of botulism begin to manifest 12 - 36 hours after ingestion of toxin contaminated food. The patient presents with the following signs and symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nausea and vomiting</li>
<li>Dizziness and tinnitus</li>
<li>Seeing double images (diplopia)</li>
<li>Inability to speak clearly (dysphasia)</li>
<li>Difficulty swallowing (dysphagia)</li>
<li>Difficulty breathing (dyspnoea)</li>
<li>Muscle weakness (neck, limbs, respiratory)</li>
<li>Death may occur from sudden respiratory paralysis and airway obstruction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diagnosis is difficult when only one person is affected because the signs of botulism are similar to those of acute polio, myasthenia gravis and Guillain-Barre syndrome. However, diagnosis can be made when a group of people who had consumed the same food (especially tinned or canned foods) suffers from the same</p>
<p>neurological symptoms without mental confusion or loss of awareness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main cause of death in botulism is respiratory failure. The patient therefore must be managed in a high-dependence unit. A tracheostomy is performed and mechanical respirator used. Cleansing enemas are administered to remove unabsorbed toxin from the colon and botulinum autotoxin serum is given and repeated after two to four hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-points-would-you-emphasise-when-giving-a-health-education-talk-on-prevention-of-bacterial-food-poisoning">What points would you emphasise when giving a health education talk on prevention of bacterial food poisoning?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-points-would-you-emphasise-when-giving-a-health-education-talk-on-prevention-of-bacterial-food-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your list should include the following preventative measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health education to encourage people to serve meals immediately they are prepared in order to prevent growth of organisms, such as staphylococci</li>
<li>Keeping food covered to keep off dust and rodents</li>
<li>Thorough reheating of left over foods (to kill toxins food must be heated to over <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>140</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">140^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">14</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>)</li>
<li>Excluding persons with skin infections from food handling</li>
<li>Refrigerating cooked food</li>
<li>Keeping the kitchen and cooling areas clean</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>SECTION 6: AIRBORNE DISEASES</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>In this section you are going to learn about those communicable diseases whose main route of transmission is the air you breathe. That is, the organisms which cause these diseases enter the body through the respiratory tract. Most respiratory tract infections are airborne diseases. In module one unit four on paediatric nursing, you covered quite a number of respiratory tract diseases. Can you remember which ones were covered?</p>
<p>List the respiratory tract diseases you learnt in the unit on paediatric nursing.</p>
<p>In module one unit four on paediatric nursing, you covered Acute Respiratory Infections (ARI), streptococcal sore throat, Acute Laryngo-Tracheal Bronchitis (ALTB) and pneumonia.</p>
<p>In this section you will look at other airborne diseases, namely: influenza, measles, whooping cough, mumps, chickenpox, meningococcal meningitis, tuberculosis and leprosy.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>List at least eight common airborne diseases</li>
<li>Describe the methods used to interrupt transmission cycles of airborne diseases</li>
<li>Describe the clinical features of airborne disease</li>
<li>Describe the management of airborne diseases</li>
<li>Explain the preventive measures of airborne diseases namely: influenza, measles, whooping cough, mumps, chickenpox, meningococcal meningitis, tuberculosis and leprosy</li>
</ul>
<p>Airborne Diseases</p>
<p>Airborne diseases have remained a major public health challenge in Eastern Africa. As mentioned in the introduction to this section, the organisms which cause these diseases enter the body through the respiratory tract.</p>
<p>When a patient or carrier of pathogens talks, coughs, laughs or sneezes, droplets of fluid are discharged into the air. The smallest of these droplets remain in the air for some time and may be inhaled by a new host. The bigger droplets fall to the ground and mix with the dust.</p>
<p>Some organisms survive the drying conditions and may be inhaled with the dust. Once they get into the body, they may affect the immediate organs involved in respiration, for example, nose and lungs, or they may pass through and spread to the blood or other distant organs like the brain or middle ear.</p>
<p>Overcrowded conditions such as congested houses, classrooms and public transport vehicles (matatus, buses and commuter trains), make the spread of these diseases very easy. Therefore, good ventilation and good manners such as covering one's mouth when sneezing or coughing can go a long way to reduce transmission of these diseases.</p>
<p>Influenza</p>
<p>This is an acute viral infection of the respiratory tract caused by any one of the three strains of the influenza viruses, types A, B and C. Influenza occurs in all countries of the world. It has a high attack rate with high mortality rates, especially among the elderly and those suffering from chronic illness such as diabetes, kidney and</p>
<p>heart disease.</p>
<p>Influenza viruses are also found in domestic animals (dogs, horses, pigs, ducks and chicken) and wild birds. Influenza spreads rapidly. Mortality is caused by secondary bacterial infections of the respiratory tract.</p>
<p>Mode of Transmission</p>
<p>The viruses are transmitted through secretions from the respiratory tract of an infected person. A susceptible host may be infected by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Direct contact with secretions from an infected person</li>
<li>Inhaling droplets secreted when an infected person sneezes, coughs or talks</li>
<li>Handling contaminated handkerchiefs and other articles belonging to an infected person</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 132 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 133 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The signs and symptoms of influenza include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sudden onset of fever (39°C - 40°C)</li>
<li>Malaise and prostration</li>
<li>Sore throat</li>
<li>Coughing</li>
<li>Running nose (rhinorrhoea)</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Muscle pain (myalgia)</li>
<li>Nausea and vomiting</li>
<li>Abdominal pain</li>
<li>Diarrhoea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Some of the common complications of influenza are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pneumonia</li>
<li>Chronic bronchitis</li>
<li>Myocarditis</li>
<li>Meningitis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As with many viral diseases, there is no specific treatment. You should prescribe bed rest and give paracetamol to relieve pain and fever. Prophylactic broad spectrum antibiotics may also be prescribed to prevent secondary bacterial infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Since the infective particles are spread by droplets from patients or carriers, an important part of the control of this disease is based on preventing droplets from being inhaled by others. That is, people must not inhale 'second-hand' air.</p>
<p>This can be achieved through the following measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>Avoiding overcrowded places especially where ventilation is poor</li>
<li>Immunisation using anti-influenza vaccine about once every year</li>
<li>Avoiding close contact with an infected person or handling the patient's personal articles, such as handkerchiefs</li>
<li>Covering one's mouth when coughing or sneezing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="measles-morbili-rubeola">Measles (Morbili, Rubeola)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measles-morbili-rubeola" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is an acute and highly contagious disease that mainly affects children. Measles is a major cause of child mortality in less developed countries such as Kenya. Together with pneumonia it accounts for about a quarter of all deaths occurring in hospitals in Eastern Africa.</p>
<p>Non-immunised and malnourished children under the age of three years are at high risk of contracting measles. The severity of measles is related to the viral load one gets from the source. That is, children who live in overcrowded dwellings and who are in close contact with the index case for the whole infective period obtain a high dose of the virus. Such children develop severe measles with high case fatality rates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The measles virus spreads through invisible droplets secreted from the respiratory tract of an infected person. Measles spreads very easily and fast. The virus infects the skin and the layer of cells that line the lungs, gastrointestinal tract, eyes, mouth and throat. In addition, the measles virus weakens the child's immune system for many weeks after the onset of the illness, leaving the child at risk of other infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The clinical features of measles depends on the nutritional status of the affected child. The skin rash of measles is characteristic and is said to 'match' from one region of the body to another in a systematic way. It begins on the face and neck, then spreads to the chest and abdomen after 24 hours. On the third day, the rash spreads to the arms and lower limbs. Depending on the nutritional status of a child, measles can either be complicated or uncomplicated.</p>
<p>Uncomplicated measles generally occurs in well-nourished or slightly underweight children. It presents with the following signs and symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Conjunctivitis</li>
<li>Rhinitis</li>
<li>Coughing</li>
<li>Koplik's spots</li>
<li>Stomatitis</li>
<li>Skin rash</li>
</ul>
<p>All these may disappear after a few days with or without treatment.</p>
<p>Complicated measles occurs in malnourished children and those who are underweight. It presents with the following signs and symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nasal flaring</li>
<li>Rapid respiration (pneumonia)</li>
<li>Dyspnoea</li>
<li>Hoarse voice (laryngitis)</li>
<li>Barking cough</li>
<li>Inspiratory stridor</li>
<li>Skin rash</li>
<li>Loss of interest to feed</li>
<li>Vomiting (this causes malnutrition)</li>
<li>Diarrhoea (gastroenteritis)</li>
<li>Dryness of eyes, hazy cornea (keratitis)</li>
<li>Photophobia (encephalitis)</li>
<li>Convulsions</li>
<li>Ear discharge (otitis media)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The diagnosis of measles is usually based on the following signs and symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>WHO Diagnostic criteria:</li>
<li>Rash of three or more days</li>
<li>Fever of 38°C or higher</li>
<li>Presence of 3Cs: coryza, cough and conjunctivitis</li>
<li>Febrile xanthema in which there are red eyes and a cough</li>
<li>Typical skin rash ('matching' skin rash)</li>
<li>Koplik's spots</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Uncomplicated measles is usually treated on an outpatient basis. You should advise the mother to give the child adequate fluids, a light nutritious diet, and paracetamol for pain and fever.</p>
<p>Give a single dose of vitamin A 200,000iu in order to speed up recovery from measles and prevent the development of complications. Also, advise the mother to bring the child to the clinic everyday for follow up.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Weigh all children suffering from measles.</p>
<p>In the case of complicated measles, you should admit the child to hospital and give them a balanced diet to improve their nutritional status.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-five-complications-of-measles-that-you-have-come-across">List five complications of measles that you have come across.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-five-complications-of-measles-that-you-have-come-across" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should watch out for the following complications and treat them accordingly.</p>
<ul>
<li>Convulsions: give anti-convulsants</li>
<li>Gastroenteritis: give oral rehydration</li>
<li>Xerophthalmia: give vitamin A 200,000 units</li>
<li>Meningitis, pneumonia, conjunctivitis, otitis media: give broad spectrum antibiotics</li>
<li>Fever: give antipyretics and apply fever reduction measures such as tepid sponging</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The only successful method of preventing measles and its serious complications is immunisation. This should be given to all children from the age of nine months; both the healthy and the sick who have not been previously immunised.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="whooping-cough-pertussis">Whooping Cough (Pertussis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#whooping-cough-pertussis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an acute infectious disease of the respiratory tract caused by bacteria of the genus bordetella called bordetella pertussis. Whooping cough is also known as pertusssis.</p>
<p>The disease causes production of very sticky mucus that blocks the lumen of the bronchioles. This leads to a persistent cough in an attempt to get rid of the mucus. Usually, the cough occurs after feeding thereby causing the child to vomit. This robs the child of the little breast milk or food they may have eaten thus causing them to be malnourished. Mortality from whooping cough is highest in children aged one year or less.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is spread by droplets from secretions of the upper respiratory tract. The disease can also be spread by direct contact with freshly contaminated objects.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incubation period of the disease ranges from six to ten days after infection, after which the clinical features appear. In babies aged three months or less, there is no 'whoop' experienced during coughing. As such the diagnosis may be missed. The characteristic 'whoop' is seen in children over three months of age. Whooping cough progresses through three stages as follows.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 135 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="catarrhal-stage">Catarrhal Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#catarrhal-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This stage begins after the incubation period and lasts for one to two weeks. The patient has slight fever and a cough that is troublesome especially at night. The cough often ends with vomiting. Gradually the cough becomes paroxysmal in character with a running nose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paroxysmal-stage">Paroxysmal Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paroxysmal-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During this stage, the fever and the running nose disappear but the cough becomes more troublesome. The cough occurs in paroxysms. The child coughs with his mouth open and tongue protruding out. This severe persistent cough causes cyanosis, protrusion of eyeballs, congestion of face and neck veins, sweating, and exhaustion. The patient may vomit suddenly, pass urine or stool, bleed from the nose, bite their tongue or suffer convulsions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="convalescent-stage">Convalescent Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#convalescent-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most patients improve gradually within one to three weeks, but some patients may continue to have paroxysms of coughing for months.</p>
<p>If whooping cough is not treated it can lead to a number of complications:</p>
<ul>
<li>Inguinal hernia</li>
<li>Broncho-pneumonia</li>
<li>Collapse of the lung (atelectasis)</li>
<li>Convulsions</li>
<li>Rectal prolapse</li>
<li>Sub-conjunctival haemorrhage</li>
<li>Pneumothorax</li>
<li>Surgical emphysema</li>
<li>Retinal detachment (which may lead to blindness)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diagnosis of whooping cough is made through a postnasal swab for culture and sensitivity of bordetella pertussis and clinical symptoms (paroxysmal cough with a 'whoop').</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Young babies do not 'whoop'.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of whooping cough requires supportive treatment such as good nutrition, plenty of fluid intake and avoidance of factors which provoke coughing. Broad-spectrum antibiotics are also given to kill the pertussis organisms. However, antibiotic therapy does not shorten the paroxysmal stage of the disease.</p>
<p>You should also avoid giving sedatives and cough suppressants because they may make the illness worse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Just like in the case of measles, the only way to control whooping cough is by high immunisation coverage. To prevent whooping cough three doses of the pentavalent vaccine, starting at the age of six weeks is currently being administered. It is given at intervals of four weeks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-is-the-administration-of-the-vaccine-started-so-early">Why is the administration of the vaccine started so early?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-is-the-administration-of-the-vaccine-started-so-early" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is because very little or no passive immunity is inherited from the mother, yet it is in the first three months of life that whooping cough has a high mortality rate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mumps-epidemic-parotitis">Mumps (Epidemic Parotitis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mumps-epidemic-parotitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an acute viral disease, which usually affects school aged children and is characterised by fever and painful swelling of the salivary glands.</p>
<p>Mumps is not a major cause of death, but if contracted after puberty it can cause infertility due to its effect on the testis and ovaries. Other rare complications of mumps include; meningitis, encephalitis, pancreatitis, thyroiditis and unilateral deafness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The virus is transmitted by droplets and by direct contact with the saliva of an infected person, or indirectly through freshly contaminated articles. The incubation period is 17 - 19 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The general signs and symptoms of mumps are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Sore throat</li>
<li>Fever (pyrexia)</li>
<li>Difficulty in swallowing</li>
<li>Swelling and tenderness of salivary glands</li>
</ul>
<p>There is no rash and the fever and swelling disappear after a few days. However, in some patients complications do develop.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="orchitis">Orchitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orchitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a very common complication which occurs in about 20% of post-pubertal males. Orchitis is usually</p>
<p>unilateral. The fever returns and the testis become swollen and painful. The affected testis may atrophy leading to infertility. In girls, oophoritis may develop. It is less common than orchitis. The child complains of severe lower abdominal pain and vomiting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pancreatitis">Pancreatitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pancreatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pancreatitis may occur but it is not common. It presents with severe upper abdominal pain, fever and vomiting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meningitis">Meningitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a common complication of mumps. It presents with fever, headache, vomiting, neck rigidity and spinal rigidity. The condition resolves spontaneously.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="encephalitis">Encephalitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#encephalitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is rare and may occur with or without meningitis. The patient presents with disturbed behaviour, drowsiness, convulsions, and coma. Mumps encephalitis is a serious condition, and has a mortality rate of 2%.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The treatment of mumps is supportive and includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Analgesics/antipyretics</li>
<li>Nutritious fluid diet</li>
<li>Regular mouth washes</li>
<li>Bed rest preferably at home</li>
<li>Scrotal support for orchitis</li>
<li>Corticosteroid therapy to reduce swelling and pain of orchitis (oral prednisolone 40mg od. for four days)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It can be prevented by the administration of live attenuated mumps vaccines where it is available. This live attenuated vaccine is combined with measles and rubella.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chickenpox-varicella">Chickenpox (Varicella)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chickenpox-varicella" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a mild viral disease characterised mainly by a skin rash. It mainly affects children under ten years of age and its case fatality is very low. The causative organism is the Varicella-Zoster Virus (VZV). Chickenpox is highly contagious. An adult person who becomes infected suffers a severe form of the illness. Once a person develops chickenpox they develop immunity against the disease. However, the virus stays within the body and may reappear as herpes zoster (shingles) when the immunity of a person is weakened, for example in AIDS and diabetes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The virus is spread by droplets from the upper respiratory tract or from the discharges of ruptured lesions on the skin.</p>
<p>The incubation period is 14 - 21 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The disease begins with mild fever, sore throat and a sore palate. After two days, a characteristic rash appears on the trunk, and within a few hours, the rash spreads to the face, axilla, and scalp, and sometimes to the arms and legs. The rash vesicles are superficial. The infection usually clears spontaneously and the vesicles usually collapse and dry after three to four days, leaving skin spots but no scars. The spots clear after a while. Complications usually do not occur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The treatment of chickenpox is symptomatic. Give the patient calamine lotion to relieve itching. A local antiseptic can also be given for infected skin lesions for example chlorhexidine (hibiscrub, hibitane).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chickenpox is a self-limiting non-fatal disease. Healthy school children should be kept off school if there is an outbreak among schoolmates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meningococcal-meningitis-epidemic-meningitis">Meningococcal Meningitis (Epidemic Meningitis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningococcal-meningitis-epidemic-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an acute and dangerous bacterial disease, which occurs sporadically and in epidemics. The causative bacterium is the neisseria meningitides, also known as meningococcus. There are two types of meningitis.</p>
<p>The first type known as meningococcal meningitis is spread by droplets from one person to another and may cause epidemics in crowded institutions such as army barracks, boarding schools, prisons and camps.</p>
<p>The second type is caused by a variety of other organisms usually occurring as a complication of</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>some other disease in the body, or by direct extension from neighbouring structures such as the middle ear (otitis media). This type of meningitis occurs one case at a time, that is, it is sporadic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>About 20 - 25% of people may be healthy carriers of the meningococcus and the other organisms which cause meningitis, such as, haemophilus influenzae type B and streptococcus pneumoniae (pneumococci). Transmission of the neisseria meningitides occurs by direct contact and by droplets from nasal and throat discharges of infected persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When a susceptible host is infected the organism causes blood poisoning (septicaemia) and pyogenic meningitis. The onset is sudden with the following signs and symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Severe headache and neck rigidity</li>
<li>Fever and rigors</li>
<li>Pain in the back and limbs</li>
<li>Irritability and confusion</li>
<li>Drowsiness and coma</li>
<li>Positive Kernig's and Brudzinki's signs</li>
<li>On lumbar puncture, Cerebral Spinal Fluid (CSF) is under pressure and contains high levels of White Blood Cells (WBCs), has raised protein and lowered glucose</li>
<li>Petechial haemorrhages</li>
<li>Circulatory collapse (Waterhouse-Friderichson syndrome)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following tests are useful to confirm a diagnosis:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lumbar puncture</li>
<li>Positive Kernig's sign</li>
<li>Positive Brudzinki's 1 and 2 signs</li>
<li>Blood culture for neisseria meningitides</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient must be admitted in the hospital and antibiotic therapy started immediately. Either one of the following drugs can be given:</p>
<ul>
<li>IM crystalline penicillin (benzyl penicillin) six mega units stat followed by three mega units every six hours</li>
<li>IM chloramphenicol 500mg every six hours</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260116-cf8f16bd.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The prevention of meningitis follows the same principles that were covered in the other airborne diseases. They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improvement in housing: adequate space, good ventilation</li>
<li>Proper disposal of respiratory secretions</li>
<li>Health education to avoid overcrowding in poorly ventilated houses</li>
<li>Isolation of the suspected patients</li>
<li>Notifying the District Medical Officer of Health</li>
<li>Immunisation during epidemics using meningitis A and C vaccine</li>
<li>Chemoprophylaxis (single dose of oral floxacillin 500mg or rifampicin) for all household and other contacts of the patient including the health care workers</li>
<li>Use of gowns, gloves and masks while caring for these patients</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tuberculosis-koch-s-disease">Tuberculosis (Koch's Disease)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tuberculosis-koch-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tuberculosis (also known as Koch's disease) is a chronic bacterial infection caused by bacteria that belongs to the family of mycobacterium. These are mycobacterium tuberculosis, mycobacterium bovis and mycobacterium</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>avium. The lungs are affected in most cases, but other organs such as the skin, bones, brain, lymph nodes, and intestine are also affected (extra-pulmonary tuberculosis).</p>
<p>Tuberculosis is found in all parts of the world and affects all age groups and sexes equally. If untreated, tuberculosis causes death and severe disability. After many years of immunising children against tuberculosis with the BCG vaccine, tuberculosis was almost controlled. However, the HIV infection which can lead to AIDS has led to the resurgence of tuberculosis. The cases of AIDS related tuberculosis have risen and continue to rise. The prevalence of tuberculosis increases as social and economic status decrease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tuberculosis is spread from an infected person to a healthy susceptible host by droplet infection. This happens when a person with pulmonary TB coughs out heavily infected sputum into the air. Though many people may thus become exposed to TB infection, only a few will progress to develop actual disease. This is because the majority have acquired active natural immunity to the disease. However if this immunity is depressed by for example, age or HIV infection, tuberculosis may flare up again and cause obvious clinical disease.</p>
<p>As mentioned earlier, there are three organisms that cause tuberculosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mycobacterium-tuberculosis">Mycobacterium Tuberculosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mycobacterium-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the main cause of pulmonary tuberculosis and extra-pulmonary tuberculosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mycobacterium-bovis">Mycobacterium Bovis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mycobacterium-bovis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This causes disease in cattle and is spread to humans through infected milk. It also causes extra-pulmonary tuberculosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mycobacterium-avium">Mycobacterium Avium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mycobacterium-avium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This causes disease in birds. Bird droppings spread pulmonary tuberculosis in individuals whose immunity is depressed (opportunistic mycobacterium).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-tuberculosis">Types of Tuberculosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>List down three types of tuberculosis?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The clinical features of tuberculosis can be divided according to the early and late signs and symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-signs-and-symptoms-of-tuberculosis">Early Signs and Symptoms of Tuberculosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-signs-and-symptoms-of-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Productive cough lasting three or more weeks</li>
<li>Night sweats</li>
<li>Unexplained weight loss</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Evening fever (pyrexia)</li>
<li>Positive tuberculin test</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="late-signs-and-symptoms-of-tuberculosis">Late Signs and Symptoms of Tuberculosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-signs-and-symptoms-of-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Coughing blood stained sputum (haemoptysis)</li>
<li>Difficulty breathing</li>
<li>Enlargement of lymph nodes</li>
<li>Extreme loss of weight</li>
<li>Signs and symptoms of other body organs affected for example meningitis, pleurisy, pericarditis, peritonitis and pleural effusion</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>TB bacteria are shed in the air in droplets whenever a patient coughs, sneezes, talks or even breathes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-diagnose-tuberculosis">How to Diagnose Tuberculosis?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-diagnose-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The best way to diagnose tuberculosis is by means of a direct sputum smear examination (Acid Fast Bacilli - AFB test) in the laboratory. If possible, at least three early morning specimens must be examined within two days. Other tests include skin tests such as the Mantoux test and chest x-rays.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Kenya National Leprosy and Tuberculosis Programme (NLTP) coordinate the treatment of tuberculosis and leprosy. The NLTP, which is a Ministry of Health project, has developed the treatment guidelines for these two diseases. Treatment regimen for tuberculosis depends on the type of tuberculosis as well as the age of patient.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The drugs used for the treatment of tuberculosis are abbreviated as follows:</p>
<p>S-streptomycin</p>
<p>E-ethambutol(plain400mgtablet)</p>
<p>H - isoniazid (150g combined with ethambutol 400mg,tablet)</p>
<p>R-rifampicin(tabletorcapsule)</p>
<p>Z-pyrazinamide(500mgtablet)</p>
<p>rifater (rhz): a combination of rifampicin 120mg, isoniazid 50mg and pyrazinamide 300mg</p>
<p>rifinah (rh): a combination of rifampicin 150mg andisoniazid100mg</p>
<p>ethizide: a combination of ethambutol 400mg and isoniazid 150mg</p>
<p>The following gives guidelines on dosages for anti-tuberculosis drugs as set down in the National Leprosy and Tuberculosis Programme (NLTP), Diagnostic Flow Chart for Pulmonary Tuberculosis.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-regimen">First Regimen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-regimen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>2ERHZ/6EH</li>
<li>Intensive therapy phase &gt; 2ERHZ</li>
<li>Continuation therapy phase &gt;6EH</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-regimen">Second Regimen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-regimen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
